Q: Mashair Railway that opened in 2010 connecting the sites of Mina, Muzdalifah and Mount Arafat serves the visitors of what city? A: Mecca (metro)
Q: The Maasai Mara National Reserve in Kenya is contiguous with what famed national park of Tanzania? A: Serengeti
Q: What second-most populous nation in Africa is also the most populous landlocked nation in the world? A: Ethiopia
Q: The Wagah border often called the 'Berlin wall of Asia' is the only road border crossing between what two countries? A: India and Pakistan
Q: Which city's site was said to have been chosen by monks following the principles of feng shui for King Taejo, founder of the Joseon/Choson dynasty in 1394? A: Seoul
Q: The design of what magnificent 12th century complex, the largest of its kind in the world, represents the home of the Gods in Hindu mythology? A: Angkor Wat

Q: What NATO country with a unique geographic position is the only one with no standing army? No navy either! A: Iceland

Q: Cape Churchill in Wapusk National Park, Canada is renowned as the best location in the world to view what? A: Polar bears
Q: The economic grouping acronym BRIC that referred to Brazil, Russia, India and China was changed to BRICS in 2011 to include what country? A: South Africa
Q: With an average ground level of 1.5 meters above sea level, what Asian island nation is the lowest country in the world? (hint: it is also the smallest Asian country in both population and land area) A: Maldives
Q: Among hundreds of animal paintings, the only figure of a human being appears in an engraving called Shaft of the Dead Man at what World Heritage location? A: Lascaux caves
Q: What wild American feature begins at Springer Mountain in Georgia and ends at Katahdin in Maine for a total distance of 2,175 miles? A: Appalachian Trail
Q: Francophonie is an international organization of 56 member states where there is a notable affiliation with the French language. What is the largest country in this group? A: Canada
Q: The artificial Gatun Lake that was created between 1907 and 1913 forms a major component of what water body? A: Panama Canal
Q: A funnel cloud is nothing but condensed water droplets associated with a rotating column of wind which extends from the base of a cloud without touching the ground. If it touches the ground, what is it called? A: Tornado
Q: Primorsky Stairs, a stairway of 192 steps immortalized in film lore, is a formal entrance from the direction of the Black Sea into which European city? A: Odessa
Q: Juba is the capital of what autonomous African region that became an independent country on 9th July, 2011? A: South Sudan
Q: The plateau 'Cappadocia' with its spectacular landscapes, caves, and fairy chimneys is a popular tourist attraction of which country? A: Turkey
Q: In Jan 2011, Sri Lanka decided to discard all references to what British colonial name of the country from its state institutions? A: Ceylon
Q: The novel as well as the movie Girl with a Pearl Earring based on painter Vermeer's work was set in which Dutch city also known for its pottery? A: Delft
Q: Which scale that is used for measuring the intensity of an earthquake (not Richter!) quantifies its effects on humans, objects of nature, and man-made structures on a scale of I through XII with XII denoting total destruction? A: Mercalli intensity scale
Q: Located just 508 miles from the North Pole, Alert is said to be the northernmost permanently inhabited place in the world. In which Canadian province/territory is it located? A: Nunavut
Q: If the coastline paradox is ignored, which country in the world has the longest coastline? A: Canada
Q: Which magnificent Tibetan landmark escaped damage during the Cultural Revolution of China in 1966 through the personal intervention of Zhou Enlai? A: Potala Palace
Q: The Merlion, an imaginary creature with the head of a lion and the body of a fish, is used as the mascot of which tiny Asian island nation? A: Singapore

Q: Which land-locked country has the most official languages in the world at 34 including Spanish, Aymara and Quechua? A: Bolivia
Q: The US think tank Fund For Peace comes out with a Failed States Index every year. Which country topped the list for a fourth consecutive year in 2011? A: Somalia

Q: If water bodies were left out and only land area were considered, what is the second largest country in the world after Russia? A: China
Q: Landseer's Lions, a set of four sculptures of lions surround which London monument? A: Nelson's Column in Trafalgar Square
Q: 'Pha That Lung', a large gold-covered Buddhist stupa is regarded as the most important monument and national symbol in which landlocked Asian country? A: Laos
Q: Located in Micronesia and covering just 21 square kilometres, what is the world's smallest island nation? A: Nauru

Q: Which French city is home to the Palais des Papes (Palace of the Popes) where several popes and antipopes lived from the early 14th to early 15th centuries? A: Avignon

Q: Which island, the third largest in the world, is divided between Indonesia, Malaysia and Brunei? A: Borneo

Q: From the Greek for 'going downhill' and most commonly found in Antarctica and Greenland, what is the name of the wind that carries high density air from a higher elevation down a slope under the force of gravity? A: Katabatic wind

A: Decade Volcanoes

Q: During World War I, which Belgian city that was the centre of intense battles was nicknamed 'wipers'? A: Ypres
Q: Who is the Scottish outlaw of the 18th century who is sometimes called as the Scottish Robin Hood? (hint: also the name of a Manhattan like cocktail) A: Rob Roy
Q: What term refers to the stage of the journey that saw the forcible passage of Africans to the New World as part of the Atlantic slave trade? A: Middle Passage
Q: What is the name of the fictional woman who is depicted as the national emblem of the French Republic? A: Marianne
Q: As numerous countries gained their independence in that year, which year in the second half of the 20th century is known as the 'Year of Africa'? A: 1960
Q: What foreign policy theory promoted by the US government during the Cold War speculated that if one land in a region came under the influence of communism, the surrounding countries would follow? A: Domino theory
Q: What 'fruity' term for a small and unstable country dependent on agriculture was first used by O. Henry in reference to Honduras? A: Banana republic
Q: Because foreigners were forbidden to serve in the French Army after the 1830 July Revolution, what was created by Louis Philippe, the King of France in 1831? A: French Foreign Legion
Q: Mimar Sinan (1489-1588) is considered the greatest architect of the classical period and was responsible for the Suleiman mosque in Istanbul and many other magnificent constructions. Which political entity benefited from his genius? A: Ottomon empire
Q: In ancient Greece, the bematists who accompanied Alexander the Great on his campaigns were trained to measure what? A: Distances (by counting their steps)
Q: If you have to associate one person with the 'Kuomintang Party' between 1929 and 1948, who would it be? A: Chiang Kai-shek
Q: Meaning 'Apple orchard' in Spanish, what is the collective name of the ten concentration camps in California where thousands of Japanese Americans were imprisoned during WWII? A: Manzanar
Q: Ephialtes of Trachis was the traitor who showed the Persian forces a trail around the allied Greek position at the pass of Thermopylae, which helped them win the Battle of Thermopylae in 480 BC. He was portrayed as a severely deformed man in which blood-soaked 2007 movie? A: 300
Q: What are 'Potemkin villages' which were purportedly erected at the direction of Russian minister Grigori Potemkin to impress Empress Catherine II during her visit to Crimea in 1787? A: Fake settlements
Q: What was the name of the notorious biological research unit of the Japanese Army that undertook lethal human experimentation during the Second Sino-Japanese War (1937-1945) and WWII? A: Unit 731
Q: On 31 October 1984, the English actor Peter Ustinov was waiting to interview which Asian leader when that person was assassinated? A: Indira Gandhi
Q: Waitangi Day held each year on February 6 is the national day of New Zealand as a treaty instrumental in the country's history was signed at that place in 1840. The name 'Waitangi' means 'weeping waters' in which language? A: Māori
Q: Kåre Kristiansen, a member of the Nobel Committee resigned in 1994 in protest at the awarding of the Peace Prize to which person, calling the awardee a terrorist? A: Yasser Arafat
Q: Who was executed by hanging at Ramla prison in 1962 and remains the only person to have been executed by an Israeli civilian court? A: Adolf Eichmann
Q: What two countries fought the six-day 'Football War' or the '100-hours War' in 1969? A: El Salvador and Honduras
Q: What sporty term popularized by Rudyard Kipling in Kim was used to describe the rivalry between the British Empire and the Russian Empire in their quest for supremacy in Central Asia in the 19th century? A: """Great game"""
Q: Literally called 'The Righteous and Harmonious Society Movement', what is the more popular western name for the Chinese rebellion took place from 1899 to 1901 against foreign influence during the final years of the Manchu rule? A: Boxer Rebellion
Q: What generic term for all African American soldiers was originally applied to the members of the U.S. 10th Cavalry Regiment by the native Apache Indians? A: Buffalo soldiers
Q: The Temple of Artemis at Ephesus, one of the Seven Wonders of the World, was destroyed on July 21, 356 BC in an act of arson. Historian Plutarch remarked that the goddess was preoccupied with the birth of whom that occurred on the same day to save her temple? A: Alexander the Great
Q: What 1990s theory proposed by the political scientist Samuel Huntington contends that cultural and religious identities will be the primary source of conflict in the post-Cold War world? A: Clash of Civilizations
Q: What is the name of the Polish trade union founded in September 1980 at the Gdańsk Shipyard that was originally led by Lech Wałęsa? A: Solidarity
Q: In 1954, which country suggested that it should join NATO to preserve peace in Europe but this proposal was rejected as the other countries felt that it would weaken the alliance? A: Soviet Union
Q: The usage of the what derogatory phrase referring to the Ottoman Empire is attributed to Tsar Nicholas I of Russia? A: """Sick man of Europe"""
Q: What was the famous one-word reply of General McAuliffe of the US to a German demand for surrender during the Battle of the Bulge in WWII? A: """Nuts!"""
Q: In 1948, which Latin American country became the first in the world to constitutionally abolish its army? A: Costa Rica
Q: "Whose last words before he drank poison reportedly were ""Crito, we owe a cock to Asclepius. Pay it and do not neglect it.""?" A: Socrates
Q: A motto of which lethal 20th century regime was 'To keep you is no benefit. To destroy you is no loss' referring to civilian Cambodians? A: Khmer Rouge
Q: What is the name of the village on the border between North and South Korea where the 1953 armistice that halted the Korean War was signed? A: Panmunjeom
Q: What South African island was used as a gaol for political prisoners while the country was under the policy of apartheid? A: Robben Island
Q: What burning-liquid weapon was used by the Byzantine Greeks to great effect as it could continue burning even on water? A: Greek fire
Q: What weapon do many historians call 'the machine gun of the Middle Ages'? A: Longbow
Q: What two countries formed in 1993 as a result of what is known as the 'Velvet Divorce'? A: Czech Republic and Slovakia
Q: The Battle of Austerlitz, one of Napoleon's greatest victories is also known by what name that references Emperor Francis and the Russian Czar along with Napoleon himself? A: Battle of the Three Emperors
Q: Idries Shah who achieved prominence as an authority on Sufism is credited with popularizing the stories of which 13th folk figure of Turkey known for his wit and humor? A: Nasreddin Hodja
Q: "What 1945 classic satire was rejected for publication by T. S. Eliot as ""We have no conviction ... that this is the right point of view from which to criticise the political situation at the present time...""?" A: Animal Farm by George Orwell
Q: Sequels featuring which character who originally appeared in a 1913 novel were published as Glad Books from 1915 onward? A: Pollyanna
Q: The Pulitzer-nominated 1979 book The Madwoman in the Attic which examines Victorian literature from a feminist perspective takes its title from a plot point of what 1847 novel? A: Charlotte Brontë's Jane Eyre
Q: Richard Pevear and Larissa Volokhonsky a current-day husband and wife team are known for what type of contribution to literature? A: Translations
Q: "What are the first two lines of the poem Solitude by Ella Wheeler Wilcox whose next lines are shown below? "".................................................... ..................................................... For the sad old earth must borrow its mirth, But has trouble enough of its own...""" A: Laugh, and the world laughs with you; Weep, and you weep alone;

Q: According to a 1864 adventure novel, Saknussemm's Corridor in an extinct volcano in Iceland is the place to start if you seek to go where? A: Center of the earth
Q: American poet Dixon Lanier Merritt's well-known limerick is about what bird? A: Pelican

Q: Polynesia the parrot teaches animal language to what literary character? A: Doctor Doolittle

Q: The phrase 'motiveless malignity' was used by S. T. Coleridge to describe which diabolic villain of literature? A: Iago
Q: A 1978 contemplative travel book of Peter Matthiessen concerned him tracking what elusive creature of the Himalayas? A: Snow leopard
Q: A 1986 book on the pivotal role of six Cold War diplomats including Dean Acheson and George Kennan had what title evoking a certain Biblical trio? A: The Wise Men
Q: Just as Edward Bulwer-Lytton is associated with bombastic writing, what is the similarly famous poem of William McGonagall? A: The Tay Bridge Disaster
Q: In Alan Moore's graphic novel V for Vendetta the anarchist wears a mask of which real-life person? A: Guy Fawkes
Q: What French novel is said to based on an epidemic that hit the Algerian city of Oran in 1849? A: The Plague by Camus
Q: The award winning 2005 children's book And Tango Makes Three has been subject to much controversy as it was seen to be highlighting what behavior in the animal kingdom? A: Homosexuality
Q: "Whose interview in Life magazine is said to have led to an upsurge in the sales of James Bond books? After a private screening of Dr. No, he also reportedly said ""I wish I had had James Bond on my staff.""" A: JFK
Q: In technical terms, the unforgettable Jeeves of P. G. Wodehouse is a valet and not a butler. Why? A: He serves a man and not a household
Q: In March 1989, Britain and Iran broke diplomatic relations over what reason related to literature? A: Fatwa on Salman Rushdie
Q: Polydactyl cats (born with more than the usual number of toes) are associated with which writer who was known for his love for them? A: Ernest Hemingway
Q: "What sonnet of Irish poet Seamus Heaney, a tribute to a long-running bulletin from BBC, starts as ""Dogger, Rockall, Malin, Irish Sea""?" A: The Shipping Forecast
Q: What is the name of the castle in Mervyn Peake's series of fantasy novels that has now come to mean any sprawling complex? A: Gormenghast
Q: Chekov's play Three Sisters is said to have been inspired by which real life siblings? A: Brontë sisters
Q: Misselthwaite Manor is the chief locale of what beloved children's novel that tells the coming of age story of Mary Lennox? A: The Secret Garden by Frances Hodgson Burnett
Q: The year 1819 is significant for lovers of English poetry because of the publication of six famous odes by whom? A: John Keats (1795-1821)
Q: Which writer wrote the introduction for Robert Frank's influential photography book The Americans (1958) that contained images from Frank's travels across the US? A: Jack Kerouac
Q: In Strega Nona by Tomie dePaola, the children's tale of magic gone awry, a town in Italy is buried in an avalanche of what? A: Pasta
Q: What 1904 story by M. R. James in which the protagonist finds an antique artifact with undesirable consequences gets its ominously inviting title from a 1793 Robert Burns poem/song? A: Oh, Whistle, and I'll Come to You, My Lad
Q: "What 1949 American work that is now a benchmark of the ecological movement is best known for the quote ""A thing is right when it tends to preserve the integrity, stability, and beauty of the biotic community. It is wrong when it tends otherwise.""?" A: A Sand County Almanac by Aldo Leopold
Q: What 300 BC book from ancient Greece that was essential reading for students for centuries was said to be second only to the Bible in the number of editions published? A: Euclid's Elements
Q: A controversial 1994 book by psychologist Richard J. Herrnstein whose premise is that genes and environment are predictors of intelligence is titled after what statistical function? A: Bell curve
Q: The central character of which 1919 novel is the reporter George Willard to whom the denizens of a certain American Midwest town confide their secrets? A: Winesburg, Ohio by Sherwood Anderson
Q: The text of what ancient classic is a set of oracular statements represented by 64 sets of six hexagrams, with each hexagram in turn composed of six lines of Yangs or Yins? A: I Ching
Q: During the Siege of Sarajevo in the 90s, Susan Sontag directed what play in a candlelit theater symbolizing the city's absurd anticipation of western intervention? A: Samuel Beckett's Waiting for Godot

Q: If 221B Baker Street is to Sherlock Holmes, 9 Bywater Street, Chelsea is to whom? A: George Smiley
Q: London to Suez = a; Suez to Bombay = b; Bombay to Calcutta = c; Calcutta to Hong Kong = d; Hong Kong to Yokohoma = e; Yokohama to San Francisco = f; San Francisco to New York City = g; New York to London = h. In terms of 19th century adventure time, a + b + c + d + e + f + g + h = ? A: 80 days

Q: What term that is a mechanism for the disappearance of inconvenient documents comes from George Orwell's Nineteen Eighty-Four in which it is a slot into which officials deposit records to be destroyed? A: Memory hole

Q: Similar to John Reed's Ten Days that Shook the World, which influential 1930s book by Edgar Snow is an account of the Communist Party of China? A: Red Star Over China

Naipaul

The owner of the house hears this, and sends for the porter, and it is found they are both named ___. The rich ___ tells the poor ___ that he became wealthy, ""by Fortune and Fate,"" the details of which he will now proceed to relate. What magnificent adventures follow?" A: Stories of Sindbad

Q: 1. The A is the outermost of the large, bright ones. 2. The B is the largest, brightest, and most massive. 3. The C is wide but faint and located inward of the B. 4. The D is the innermost and is also very faint. 5. The E is the second outermost and is extremely wide. 6. The F is the outermost discrete one and very active. 7. The G is very thin and faint and is halfway between the F and the E. What are we talking about? A: Rings of Saturn
